function cmp (a, b) {
let pa = a.split('.');
let pb = b.split('.');
for (let i = 0; i &lt; Math.max(pa.length, pb.length); i++) {
let na = Number(pa[i]);
let nb = Number(pb[i]);
if (isNaN(na)) na = 0;
if (isNaN(nb)) nb = 0;
if (na &gt; nb) return "Older";
if (nb &gt; na) return "Newer";
}
return "Same";

			<dict>
				<key>WFCommentActionText</key>
				<string>Observation with iOS 13.3 Public beta 2 and UpdateKit v6.0.1.

The UpdateKit documentation (https://www.mikebeas.com/updatekit/docs) states that UpdateKit returns 'Installed Update', however with v6.0.1 it actually returns 'Install'. (With UpdateKit v6.0.2, this issue was corrected.)

To accommodate both 'Installed Update' and 'Install' I changed the operator to 'contains', but with that another anomaly was observered with with iOS 13.3 Public beta 2: the default 'If' operators were 'has any value' and 'does not have any value' (not the typical operators for 'Text'). I circumvented this issue by touching 'Dictionary Value' and changing the 'as Text' to 'as Rich text' and then back to 'as Text'. After toggling the 'as' values, the 'contains' (and other typical Text) operators appeared.</string>
			</dict>
